      <tr>
        <td id="L99" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="99"></td>
        <td id="LC99" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\title</span>{A model structure on the cartesian cubical sets}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L100" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="100"></td>
        <td id="LC100" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L101" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="101"></td>
        <td id="LC101" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\maketitle</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L102" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="102"></td>
        <td id="LC102" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L103" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="103"></td>
        <td id="LC103" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\noindent</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L104" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="104"></td>
        <td id="LC104" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L105" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="105"></td>
        <td id="LC105" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{The cartesian cube category}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L106" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="106"></td>
        <td id="LC106" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L107" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="107"></td>
        <td id="LC107" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We consider the cartesian cube category  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathbb</span>{C}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, defined as the free finite product category on an interval <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span> : <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-c1">\rightrightarrows</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L108" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="108"></td>
        <td id="LC108" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">As a classifying category for an algebraic theory <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathbb</span>{T} = <span class="pl-c1">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\C</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has a covariant presentation by Lawvere duality, namely as the dual of the full subcategory of finitely-generated, free <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathbb</span>{T}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-algebras <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{Alg}(<span class="pl-c1">\mathbb</span>{T})_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{fg}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In this case, the algebras are simply <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{bipointed sets} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(A, a_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, a_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and the free ones are the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{strictly} bipointed sets <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-c1">\neq</span> a_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Thus <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{Alg}(<span class="pl-c1">\mathbb</span>{T})_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{fg}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> consists of the finite, strictly bipointed sets and all bipointed maps between them.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L109" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="109"></td>
        <td id="LC109" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L110" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="110"></td>
        <td id="LC110" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L111" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="111"></td>
        <td id="LC111" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The objects of the cartesian cube category <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\C</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are themselves called cubes, and will be written <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span>[n] = <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>x_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, ..., x_n<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span> where the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>x_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> may be regarded as coordinate axes.  The arrows,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L112" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="112"></td>
        <td id="LC112" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L113" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="113"></td>
        <td id="LC113" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">f : [n] <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> [m]<span class="pl-cce">\,</span>,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L114" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="114"></td>
        <td id="LC114" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L115" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="115"></td>
        <td id="LC115" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">are then taken to be <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-tuples of elements drawn from the set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span>[n]^+ = <span class="pl-c1">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span>, x_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, ..., x_n, <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span> regarded as formal terms representing composites of faces, degeneracies, permutations, and diagonals (alternately, the arrows are arbitrary bipointed maps <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>[m]^+<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> [n]^+<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L116" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="116"></td>
        <td id="LC116" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L117" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="117"></td>
        <td id="LC117" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L118" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="118"></td>
        <td id="LC118" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L119" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="119"></td>
        <td id="LC119" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L120" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="120"></td>
        <td id="LC120" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Cubical sets}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L121" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="121"></td>
        <td id="LC121" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L122" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="122"></td>
        <td id="LC122" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L123" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="123"></td>
        <td id="LC123" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The category <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{cSet}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{cubical sets} is the category of presheaves on the cartesian cube category <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\C</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  It is generated by the representable presheaves <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y([n])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which will be written <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n = y([n])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L124" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="124"></td>
        <td id="LC124" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and called the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{standard <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-cubes}.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L125" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="125"></td>
        <td id="LC125" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L126" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="126"></td>
        <td id="LC126" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>%%%%</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L127" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="127"></td>
        <td id="LC127" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Partial map classification and the +-algebra weak factorization system}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L128" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="128"></td>
        <td id="LC128" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L129" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="129"></td>
        <td id="LC129" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Cofibrations, partial map classification, the functor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X^+<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, the awfs of +-algebras.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

        <td id="L134" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="134"></td>
        <td id="LC134" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We  first recall the specification of the trivial-cofibration/fibration WFS from <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{GS}, and show that the resulting fibrations are equivalent to those specified in the ``logical style&#39;&#39;  given in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CCHM,OP}. </td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC179" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">To make the connection to the logical style of presentation used in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CCHM,OP}, suppose we want to describe a (uniform) filling structure on an arbitrary <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f : X<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> Y<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with respect to all generating trivial cofibrations <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\epsilon</span> : <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n +_M (M<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^{n+1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>,</td>

        <td id="LC186" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">By pulling back along <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, it suffices to consider  the case <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y=<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^{n}<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> the identity map. Thus we arrive at the following local specification, expressed logically in the internal language of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\widehat\C</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, of the object of ``(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-directed) lifting structures&#39;&#39; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L^<span class="pl-c1">0</span>(P)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on a family <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P: <span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-c1">\rightarrow</span><span class="pl-c1">\Set</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span><span class="pl-cce">\,</span>:</td>

        <td id="LC204" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There is an analogous condition <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>(P)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in which <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> replaces <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> everywhere, describing (``directed&#39;&#39;)  filling from the other end of the interval.  Note that <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CCHM, OP} derive the ``filling&#39;&#39; conclusion <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{a:<span class="pl-c1">\prod</span>_{i:I}Pi} (a<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = a_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> (a |_<span class="pl-c1">\phi</span> = s)<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span> from (connections on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and) a weaker ``composition operation&#39;&#39; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{a_1:P1} a_<span class="pl-c1">1</span> |_<span class="pl-c1">\phi</span> = s_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-cce">\,</span>,<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span> but we will not take this approach.</td>

        <td id="LC252" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>which is \eqref{diagram:ppl}, extended by the counit (evaluation) $\varepsilon : \widetilde{P}\times \I \to P$ over $\I$ on the right, and with $\I^n$ replacing $1$ in order to reason externally.  The pullback of $\varepsilon$ over $\I$ along $\delta_0$ is just $\pi_0 : \widetilde{P} \to P0$.  </span></td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L253" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="253"></td>

        <td id="L267" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="267"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L268" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="268"></td>
        <td id="LC268" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>uniformly in $\I^n$ and $\phi$\,.  Transposing the span formed by $i_\phi$ and $s$ along the adjunction $\I^* \dashv \prod_{\I}$ gives the right-hand square in \eqref{diagram:pplext}, and the commutative square formed by $a_0$ and $\pi_0$ gives the rest of the data in that diagram. Thus the $L^0(P)$-structure gives an $a : \I^n\times\I\to P$ as indicated.  Looking at \eqref{diagram:pplext}, we see that $a$ lifts across $\varepsilon$ to a unique map $\overline{a} : \I^n\times\I\to \widetilde{P}\times\I$ over \I, by the universal property of $\varepsilon : \widetilde{P}\times\I \to P$.  We can therefore set $$j = \delta_0^*( \overline{a}) : \I^n \to \widetilde{P}\,.$$</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L269" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="269"></td>
        <td id="LC269" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L270" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="270"></td>
        <td id="LC270" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>Suppose conversely that we have a $\plusalgx$-structure on $\pi_0 : \widetilde{P} \to P0$, and we want to build a (0-directed) partial path-lifting structure on $P$.  Take any $\I^n, \phi, s, a_0$ as indicated and we require an $a : \I^n\times\I\to P$ over $\I$.    From $s$ we get $\overline{s}$ by the universal property of $\varepsilon$, and therefore we get $\overline{s}_0$ by pullback.   From $\overline{s}_0$ and $a_0$ and the $\plusalgx$ structure on $\pi_0$ we get a map $j : \I^n \to \widetilde{P}$ over $P0$ which is a diagonal filler of the indicated square formed by $i_\phi, \overline{s}_0, a_0$ and $\pi_0$.  We then get the required map $a : \I^n\times\I\to P$ over $\I$ as the ($\I^* \dashv \prod_{\I}$)-transpose of $j$,</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L271" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="271"></td>
        <td id="LC271" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\[</span></td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC272" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>a = \varepsilon \circ(j\times\I)\,.</span></td>
      </tr>

      <tr>
        <td id="L288" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="288"></td>
        <td id="LC288" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which is <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:ppl}, extended by the counit (evaluation) <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\varepsilon</span> : <span class="pl-c1">\widetilde</span>{P}<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on the right, and with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> still representing the domain of a variable to reason internally.  The pullback of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\varepsilon</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> along <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is then the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> : <span class="pl-c1">\widetilde</span>{P} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> P<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> that we are interested in.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L289" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="289"></td>
        <td id="LC289" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L290" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="290"></td>
        <td id="LC290" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Given an <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L^<span class="pl-c1">0</span>(P)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-structure, reasoning internally we construct a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\plusalgx</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> : <span class="pl-c1">\widetilde</span>{P} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> P<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as follows: for any cofibration <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i_<span class="pl-c1">\phi</span> : [<span class="pl-c1">\phi</span>]<span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and any commutative square,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L291" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="291"></td>
        <td id="LC291" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{equation}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{diagram:plusfiller}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L292" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="292"></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L304" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="304"></td>
        <td id="LC304" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Transposing the top left span in <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:plusfiller} formed by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i_<span class="pl-c1">\phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> along the adjunction <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^* <span class="pl-c1">\dashv</span> <span class="pl-c1">\prod</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> gives the right-hand square in <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:pplext}, and the commutative square in <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:plusfiller} formed by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> gives the rest of the data in <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:pplext}. Thus the assumed <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L^<span class="pl-c1">0</span>(P)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-structure gives an <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a : <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I\to</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as indicated in <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:pplext}.  But then <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> lifts uniquely across <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\varepsilon</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to a map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\overline</span>{a} : <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\widetilde</span>{P}<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> over <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>, by the universal property of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\varepsilon</span> : <span class="pl-c1">\widetilde</span>{P}<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We can therefore set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span>j = <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>^*( <span class="pl-c1">\overline</span>{a}) : <span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\widetilde</span>{P}<span class="pl-cce">\,</span>.<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span></td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L305" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="305"></td>
        <td id="LC305" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L306" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="306"></td>
        <td id="LC306" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Suppose conversely that we have a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\plusalgx</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> : <span class="pl-c1">\widetilde</span>{P} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> P<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and we want to build a (0-directed) lifting structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Take any <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\phi</span>, s, a_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as indicated in <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:pplext}, and we require an <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a : <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I\to</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.    From <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we get <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\overline</span>{s}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by the universal property of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\varepsilon</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and we therefore have <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\overline</span>{s}_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by pullback.   From <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\overline</span>{s}_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\plusalgx</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we obtain a map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>j : <span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\widetilde</span>{P}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> which is a diagonal filler of the indicated square formed by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i_<span class="pl-c1">\phi</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\overline</span>{s}_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, a_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Finally, we obtain the required map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a : <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I\to</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as the (<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^* <span class="pl-c1">\dashv</span> <span class="pl-c1">\prod</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>)-transpose of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>j<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>,</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L307" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="307"></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L338" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="338"></td>

</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L339" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="339"></td>
        <td id="LC339" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We make use of the Sattler model structure <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{sattler} on the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{Dedekind cubical sets} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\widehat\D</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\psh</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\D</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the category of <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{Dedekind cubes}, defined as the Lawvere theory of distributive lattices.  The unique product-preserving functor </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L340" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="340"></td>

        <td id="LC341" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">i : <span class="pl-c1">\C</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\D</span></td>

We then need to show that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is in~<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathcal</span>{W}_<span class="pl-c1">\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>

        <td id="LC410" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can apply Theorem 2.2.1 of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Hess}, with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{K} = <span class="pl-c1">\widehat\C</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{M} = <span class="pl-c1">\widehat\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>V = i_!<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>k=i^*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and:</td>

        <td id="LC414" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> factor the codiagonal <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X + X <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\circ</span> j : X + X <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span> X <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>j = (<span class="pl-c1">\partial</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span> X) : X + X <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>

        <td id="L416" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="416"></td>
        <td id="LC416" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> It remains only to show that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i_!p : <span class="pl-c1">\i</span>_!(<span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span> X) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> i_!X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathcal</span>{W}_<span class="pl-c1">\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i_!j : i_!(X + X) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> i_!(<span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span> X)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathcal</span>{C}_<span class="pl-c1">\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The latter  is clear, since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>j<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is monic. To show the former, observe that for any <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\widehat\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, the projection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span> : <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\D</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span> D <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathcal</span>{W}_<span class="pl-c1">\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by 3-for-2, since the ``cylinder end&#39;&#39; inclusion <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-c1">\to\I</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\D</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, as a pullback of an endpoint inclusion, is a cofibration, and a strong deformation retract (using the connection on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>), and hence is in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathcal</span>{W}_<span class="pl-c1">\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{GS}.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC438" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In particular, the standard <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-cube is <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span> = y([<span class="pl-c1">1</span>])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and the standard <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-cube is <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = y([<span class="pl-c1">0</span>])=<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  For any cubical set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X: <span class="pl-c1">\H</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{op} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Set</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, we shall write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X_n = X([n])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and call this the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{set of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-cubes in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>}.       </tr>

        <td id="L442" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="442"></td>
        <td id="LC442" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In particular <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n_m = <span class="pl-c1">\H</span>([m],[n])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the set of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-cubes in the standard <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-cube.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC447" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We now have <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^m <span class="pl-c1">\cong</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^{n+m}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, in virtue of the preservation of products by the Yoneda embedding.</td>

        <td id="L451" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="451"></td>
        <td id="LC451" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proposition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L452" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="452"></td>
        <td id="LC452" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The category <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\HH</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of hypercubical sets is the classifying topos for <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{strictly} bipointed objects.  A strictly bipointed object in a topos <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathcal</span>{E}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is an object <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> together with points <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, a_<span class="pl-c1">1</span> : <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, with the property that the equalizer <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>[a_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = a_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>] <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is isomorphic to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L453" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="453"></td>
        <td id="LC453" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{proposition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L454" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="454"></td>
        <td id="LC454" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L455" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="455"></td>
        <td id="LC455" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L456" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="456"></td>
        <td id="LC456" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Consider the covariant presentation $\HH = \Set^\B$, where as in \ref{subsubsec:covariant}, $\B$ is the category of finite, strictly bipointed sets and bipointed maps, now written simply $f: [m]\to [n]$ (i.e.\ dropping the special covariant notation $[n]^+$).  We can extend $\B\to\B_=$ by freely adjoining coequalizers, making $\B_=$ the free finite \emph{colimit} category on a co-bipointed object. An explicit presentation of $\B_=$ is as the finite bipointed sets, including those with $0=1$.  Write $(n)$ for the bipointed set $\{x_1, ..., x_n, 0=1\}$, with $n$ (non-constant) elements and a further element $0=1$.  There is an evident coequalizer $[1]\rightrightarrows [n]\to(n)$, which just identifies the distinguished points $0$ and $1$, and every coqualizer has either the form $[m]\rightrightarrows [n]\to [k]$ or $[m]\rightrightarrows [n]\to(k)$, for a suitable choice of $k$.  Note that there are no maps of the form $(m)\to [n]$, and that every map $[m]\to (n)$ factors uniquely as $[m]\to (m)\to (n)$ with  $[m]\to(m)$ the coequalizer of $0$ and $1$.  Thus the category $\B_=$ can be decomposed into two ``levels&#39;&#39;, the upper one of which is essentially $\B$, the lower one consisting of just the objects $(n)$ and thus essentially the finite \emph{pointed} sets, and for each $n$, there is the canonical map $[n]\to(n)$ going from top to bottom:</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC488" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u_* : <span class="pl-c1">\Set</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\B</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Set</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\B</span>_=}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is evidently full and faithful, it is the inclusion part of a sheaf subtopos <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{sh}(<span class="pl-c1">\B</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{op}_=, j) <span class="pl-c1">\hook</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Set</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\B</span>_=}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for a suitable Grothendieck topology <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>j<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\B</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{op}_=<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.         <td id="LC494" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">fitting into an equalizer <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>[<span class="pl-c1">0</span>=<span class="pl-c1">1</span>] <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rightrightarrows</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> which is the image under Yoneda of the canonical coequalizer <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>] <span class="pl-c1">\rightrightarrows</span> [<span class="pl-c1">0</span>]<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> (<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\B</span>_=<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.       <tr>
        <td id="L495" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="495"></td>
        <td id="LC495" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">forcing the sequent <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">0</span>=<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\vdash</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bot</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to hold.  Recall from Proposition 3.53 of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{JohnstoneTT} the following simple characterization of the sheaves for a closed topology generated by an object <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U<span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: an object <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a sheaf iff <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> U <span class="pl-c1">\cong</span> U<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. In the present case, it therefore suffices to show that for any <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P:<span class="pl-c1">\B</span>_= <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Set</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we have:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L496" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="496"></td>
        <td id="LC496" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L497" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="497"></td>
        <td id="LC497" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">P<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> [0=1] <span class="pl-c1">\cong</span> [0=1] <span class="pl-c1">\quad\text</span>{iff}<span class="pl-c1">\quad</span> P(n) = 1<span class="pl-cce">\ </span><span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{for all <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>}.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L498" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="498"></td>

        <td id="LC519" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We therefore have that the presheaf topos <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Set</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\B</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the closed complement sheaf subtopos of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Set</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\B</span>_=}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> given by forcing the sequent <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-c1">\neq</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.         <td id="LC530" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This can be shown directly by standard methods, but it also follows immediately by composing the inverse image of the geometric morphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{sSets} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\HH</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> classifying the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-simplex <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Delta</span>(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in simplicial sets, with the geometric realization <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{sSets} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{Top}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, each of which are known to preserve finite products.</td>

        <td id="L534" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="534"></td>
        <td id="LC534" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\H</span><span class="pl-cce">\ </span><span class="pl-c1">\to</span><span class="pl-cce">\ </span> <span class="pl-c1">\Cat</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the unique product-preserving functor taking <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>] <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bbtwo</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bbtwo</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the ``one arrow category&#39;&#39; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-c1">\rightarrow</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This functor takes <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>[n] <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bbtwo</span>^n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-fold product in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Cat</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>), and maps <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>[m] <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> [n]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>  to the corresponding monotone maps of the posets <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bbtwo</span>^n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The  <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{(hypercubical) nerve} functor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span>N : <span class="pl-c1">\Cat</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\HH</span><span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span> is then defined by:</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L545" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="545"></td>
        <td id="LC545" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Given categories <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\C</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and functors <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>F, G : <span class="pl-c1">\C\to\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, suppose <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>F(f) <span class="pl-c1">\neq</span> G(f)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for some <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f : A<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\C</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Take <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f^{<span class="pl-c1">\sharp</span>} : <span class="pl-c1">\bbtwo</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\C</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with image~<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Then <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>N(F)_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>(f^<span class="pl-c1">\sharp</span>) = F(f) <span class="pl-c1">\neq</span> G(f) = N(G)_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>(f^<span class="pl-c1">\sharp</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and so <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>N(F) <span class="pl-c1">\neq</span> N(G) : N(<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>)<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> N(<span class="pl-c1">\D</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  So <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>N<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is faithful.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L546" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="546"></td>
        <td id="LC546" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L547" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="547"></td>
        <td id="LC547" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For fullness, let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\varphi</span> : N(<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> N(<span class="pl-c1">\D</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a natural transformation, and define a proposed functor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>F : <span class="pl-c1">\C\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\D</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L548" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="548"></td>
        <td id="LC548" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L549" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="549"></td>
        <td id="LC549" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">F_0 = <span class="pl-c1">\varphi</span>_0 &amp;: <span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_0 = N(<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>)_0 <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> N(<span class="pl-c1">\D</span>)_0 = <span class="pl-c1">\D</span>_0<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L550" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="550"></td>
        <td id="LC550" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">F_1 = <span class="pl-c1">\varphi</span>_1 &amp;: <span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_1 = N(<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>)_1 <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> N(<span class="pl-c1">\D</span>)_1 = <span class="pl-c1">\D</span>_1.</td>

      </tr>

        <td id="LC560" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Here <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>!^* : <span class="pl-c1">\Cat</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bbtwo</span>^<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\C</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Cat</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bbtwo</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\C</span>) <span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is precomposition with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>! : <span class="pl-c1">\bbtwo</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\bbtwo</span>^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rightarrow</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bbtwo</span>^<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\mathbbm</span>{1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, so the diagram commutes. For any composable pair of arrows <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A <span class="pl-c1">\stackrel</span>{f}{<span class="pl-c1">\to</span>} B <span class="pl-c1">\stackrel</span>{g}{<span class="pl-c1">\to</span>} C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\C</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> there is a commutative square </td>

        <td id="L594" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="594"></td>
        <td id="LC594" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{corollary}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{cor:rightadjpath}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L595" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="595"></td>
        <td id="LC595" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The functor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> X^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has a <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{right} adjoint.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L596" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="596"></td>
        <td id="LC596" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{corollary}</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L597" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="597"></td>
        <td id="LC597" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L598" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="598"></td>
        <td id="LC598" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The functor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> X^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is given by precomposition with the ``successor&#39;&#39; functor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S : <span class="pl-c1">\H\to\H</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S[n] = [n+<span class="pl-c1">1</span>]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Thus <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>([n]) = X(S[n]) = (S^*(X))([n])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Precomposition always has a right adjoint <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^* <span class="pl-c1">\dashv</span> S_*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which can be calculated as:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L599" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="599"></td>
        <td id="LC599" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L600" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="600"></td>
        <td id="LC600" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">S_*(X)(n) <span class="pl-c1">\cong</span> <span class="pl-c1">\hom</span>(y[n], S_*X) <span class="pl-c1">\cong</span> <span class="pl-c1">\hom</span>(S^*(y[n]), X)<span class="pl-cce">\ </span><span class="pl-c1">\cong</span> <span class="pl-c1">\hom</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\H</span>(S(-), [n]), X).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L601" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="601"></td>

        <td id="L646" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="646"></td>
        <td id="LC646" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There is a natural transformation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X_<span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, given by the first projection from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X_<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>(n)<span class="pl-c1">\cong</span> X(n) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> X(n-<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)^{C^n_{n-1}} <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\dots</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> X(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)^{C^n_{1}}<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> X(<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L647" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="647"></td>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L649" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="649"></td>
        <td id="LC649" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Finally, we observe that that the path object functor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> itself, as a left adjoint, preserves all <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{co}limits.  This does not hold in general in type theory, but will be a special property of the cubical model.  (Cf. Lawvere <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{ATOM} on the notion of ``tiny&#39;&#39; objects and the ``amazing right adjoint&#39;&#39;.)  </td>
      </tr>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L652" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="652"></td>
        <td id="LC652" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The cubical set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of polynomials (over the integers, say), is defined by:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L653" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="653"></td>

        <td id="LC654" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">P_n = <span class="pl-cce">\{</span> p(x_1,..., x_n)<span class="pl-cce">\ </span>|<span class="pl-cce">\ </span> <span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{polynomials in at most}<span class="pl-cce">\ </span> x_1, <span class="pl-c1">\dots</span>, x_n <span class="pl-cce">\}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L655" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="655"></td>

      </tr>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L658" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="658"></td>
        <td id="LC658" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This is a ring object in the category of cubical sets, and the interval <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-cce">\ </span>= y[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> embeds into <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L659" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="659"></td>
        <td id="LC659" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The same is true for any algebraic theory <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\T</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with two constants, such as boolean algebras: there is a cubical <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\T</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and a monic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L660" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="660"></td>
        <td id="LC660" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L661" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="661"></td>
        <td id="LC661" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\C</span>[<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>] = <span class="pl-c1">\H</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the cube category, classifying intervals, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\C</span>[<span class="pl-c1">\T</span>]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> the classifying category for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\T</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-algebras.  There is an interval <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>J<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\T</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>  consisting of the generic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\T</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-algebra and its two constants.  This <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>J<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has a classifying functor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>J : <span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\T</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, inducing functors on presheaves</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L662" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="662"></td>
        <td id="LC662" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L663" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="663"></td>
        <td id="LC663" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">J_! <span class="pl-c1">\dashv</span> J^* <span class="pl-c1">\dashv</span> J_* : <span class="pl-c1">\psh</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\psh</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\T</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L664" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="664"></td>
        <td id="LC664" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L665" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="665"></td>
        <td id="LC665" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">as usual, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>J_! <span class="pl-c1">\circ</span> <span class="pl-c1">\y</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>} =<span class="pl-cce">\ </span><span class="pl-c1">\y</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\T</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\circ</span> J<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>,  with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\y</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> the respective Yoneda embeddings.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L666" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="666"></td>

</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L667" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="667"></td>
        <td id="LC667" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can calculate:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L668" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="668"></td>

      </tr>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L670" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="670"></td>
        <td id="LC670" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">J^* J_! ( <span class="pl-c1">\I</span> )( [n] ) &amp;= J^* J_! ( Y[1] )( [n] )<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L671" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="671"></td>
        <td id="LC671" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> &amp;= J^* Y( J[1] )( [n] ) = Y( J[1] )( J[n] ) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L672" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="672"></td>
        <td id="LC672" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> &amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\T</span>( J[n] , J[1] ) = <span class="pl-c1">\T\mathrm</span>{-Alg}( J[1] , J[n] ) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L673" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="673"></td>
        <td id="LC673" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> &amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\T\mathrm</span>{-Alg}( F(1) , F(n) ) = | F(n) |,</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L674" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="674"></td>
        <td id="LC674" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{split}</td>

        <td id="L675" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="675"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L676" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="676"></td>
        <td id="LC676" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>F(n)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the free <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\T</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-algebra on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> generators.  So in the case of polynomials we indeed have </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L677" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="677"></td>
        <td id="LC677" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span>P = J^* J_! ( <span class="pl-c1">\I</span> ).<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L678" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="678"></td>
        <td id="LC678" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The unit of the adjunction <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> J^* J_! ( <span class="pl-c1">\I</span> )<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is faithful, since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>J<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> itself is faithful and therefore the left adjoint <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>J_!<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is faithful.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L679" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="679"></td>
        <td id="LC679" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a ring in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\psh</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>J_!(<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a ring in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\psh</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\T</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>J^*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is left exact.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L680" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="680"></td>
        <td id="LC680" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L681" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="681"></td>
        <td id="LC681" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A closely related example is the cubical set of ``boolean polynomials&quot;,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L682" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="682"></td>

      </tr>

      <tr>
        <td id="L688" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="688"></td>
        <td id="LC688" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Identity types and box-filling}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L689" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="689"></td>
        <td id="LC689" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L690" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="690"></td>
        <td id="LC690" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Our next goal is to give an interpretation of the identity types in the category of hypercubical sets <span class="pl-c1">\HH</span><span class="pl-cce">\ </span>that uses the path-object <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as the identity type for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This will allow us to take advantage of the  combinatorial description of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> given in Proposition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{prop:pathobject}.  We need to determine which objects <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-c1">\HH</span><span class="pl-cce">\ </span>can be used as types and which maps <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> can be used as dependent types.  We will show that the conditions expressed by the rules for identity types are related to the familiar ``box-filling&#39;&#39; or Kan-conditions.  The main result of this section is Proposition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{prop:main}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L691" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="691"></td>
        <td id="LC691" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L692" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="692"></td>
        <td id="LC692" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">To begin, recall that the usual elimination and computation rules for identity types are equivalent to the combination of the following rules.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L716" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="716"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L717" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="717"></td>
        <td id="LC717" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{con}(a,a,<span class="pl-c1">\refl</span>(a)) = <span class="pl-c1">\refl</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> a,a,<span class="pl-c1">\refl</span>(a)<span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span>) : <span class="pl-c1">\Id</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> a,a,<span class="pl-c1">\refl</span>(a)<span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> a,a,<span class="pl-c1">\refl</span>(a)<span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span>).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L718" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="718"></td>
        <td id="LC718" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L719" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="719"></td>
        <td id="LC719" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The term <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{con}(a,b,p)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is in the identity type of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{x,y:A}<span class="pl-c1">\id</span>{A}(x,y)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We will often write the transport as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span>p_*u := <span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{trans}(a,b,p,u).<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L720" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="720"></td>
        <td id="LC720" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L721" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="721"></td>
        <td id="LC721" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The contraction rule is a condition on the types; it says that the singletons <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S(x) = <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{y:A}<span class="pl-c1">\Id</span>(x,y)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are all contractible.  The transport rule is a condition on the dependent types; it says that they must respect the identity on the indexing type. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L722" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="722"></td>
        <td id="LC722" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L723" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="723"></td>
        <td id="LC723" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proposition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L724" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="724"></td>
        <td id="LC724" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">If the type <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> satisfies contraction, and the family <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span>x,y: A, z:<span class="pl-c1">\id</span>{A}(x,y)<span class="pl-c1">\vdash</span> B(x,y,z)<span class="pl-cce">\ </span><span class="pl-c1">\type</span><span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span> has transport, then the usual <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Id</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-elimination rule will also be satisfied:</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L742" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="742"></td>
        <td id="LC742" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A further condition that will need to hold in order to interpret the rules for identity types is that the type <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\id</span>{A}(x,y)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> itself is a dependent type on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and therefore satisfies transport.  From this assumption, one can prove the following strengthening of transport:</td>

      </tr>

        <td id="L757" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="757"></td>
        <td id="LC757" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Under the intended interpretation in hypercubical sets, path lifting for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>x,y:A<span class="pl-c1">\vdash</span><span class="pl-c1">\id</span>{A}(x,y)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L758" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="758"></td>
        <td id="LC758" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">already implies contraction for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Indeed, let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-c1">\in</span><span class="pl-c1">\HH</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and interpret the dependent type <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>x,y:A<span class="pl-c1">\vdash</span> <span class="pl-c1">\id</span>{A}(x,y)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as the path object <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with its projection to the two endoints <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L759" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="759"></td>

</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L760" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="760"></td>

        <td id="LC761" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">If <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> satisfies path lifting, then <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> satisfies contraction.</td>

        <td id="LC765" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Writing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>=<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Id</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and reasoning internally in <span class="pl-c1">\HH</span>, take any identity <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p: x = y<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and we need to find an identity <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{con} : <span class="pl-c1">\refl</span>(x) = p<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>)^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Such an element <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{con}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a 2-cube in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the form </td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L779" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="779"></td>
        <td id="LC779" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{con}&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is given by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{con}&#39; := <span class="pl-c1">\mathsf</span>{lift}(<span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\refl</span>(x),p<span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span>,<span class="pl-c1">\refl</span>(x))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L780" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="780"></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L781" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="781"></td>
        <td id="LC781" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Using the fact that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>)^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\cong</span> A^{(<span class="pl-c1">\I\times\I</span>)}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, we can then apply the twist map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\cong</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to transpose the cube <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:contfromtransprime} into the desired form <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:contfromtrans}.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L782" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="782"></td>
        <td id="LC782" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">It remains to check the computation rule </td>

</td>
