      <tr>
        <td id="L785" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="785"></td>
        <td id="LC785" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In light of the foregoing, we need to interpret dependent types as maps <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> that have path lifting, and the types themselves as cubical sets <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a path object projection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> satisfying that condition.  Moreover, we also want the types to have iterated path objects <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\id</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\id</span>{A}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> etc.,  and as dependent types these too should be interpreted as maps with path lifting.  We begin to analyse that condition.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L786" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="786"></td>
        <td id="LC786" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L787" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="787"></td>
        <td id="LC787" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proposition}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{prop:pathliftboxfill}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L788" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="788"></td>
        <td id="LC788" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has path lifting if and only if <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has (2-)box filling.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC799" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">there is a diagonal filler as indicated.  There are two maps <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\top</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\bot</span> : <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and the path lifting condition is required with each of these cases occurring on the left.</td>

        <td id="LC801" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">An <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{open 2-box} in the 2-cube <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is by definition a subobject <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span>_{j,e} <span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span> obtained as the union, in the poset <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{Sub}(<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, of all the face maps <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>^d_i : <span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> but one,</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L805" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="805"></td>
        <td id="LC805" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The index <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>j = <span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the coordinate in which the box is open, while <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e = <span class="pl-c1">\top</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\bot</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> indicates which face of the box is missing, top or bottom.   Because we are in the symmetric situation, where the product <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> can be twisted, it  will suffice to  consider only  boxes that are open in the first coordinate, since the others can be constructed from those.  Thus we may omit the index <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>j<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, writing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span>_e<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span>_{1,e}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. Moreover, let us write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> = {<span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>}^<span class="pl-c1">2</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\top</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sqcap</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> = {<span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>}^<span class="pl-c1">2</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\bot</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{(upper and lower) open <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-boxes} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^n, <span class="pl-c1">\sqcap</span>^n <span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are defined analogously.</td>
      </tr>

The higher identity types are determined inductively by:</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L872" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="872"></td>
        <td id="LC872" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The indexing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^<span class="pl-c1">\I</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> A = A^{<span class="pl-c1">\partial\I</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is generalized to higher dimensions as follows: the type <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Id</span>^{n}_{A} <span class="pl-c1">\cong</span> A^{<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is regarded as the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{type of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-cubes in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>}, and it will be dependent on the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{type <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^{<span class="pl-c1">\partial\I</span>^n}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of boundaries in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>}, via the ``restriction&#39;&#39; map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span>A^i : A^{<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A^{<span class="pl-c1">\partial\I</span>^n},<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span>  where the boundary <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i : <span class="pl-c1">\partial</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n <span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the union of all the face maps <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span><span class="pl-c1">\partial</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n = <span class="pl-c1">\bigcup</span>_{i, d} <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i^d.<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L873" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="873"></td>
        <td id="LC873" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">As an indexing type, it is convenient to specify <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\partial</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> inductively via the ``product rule&#39;&#39; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$$</span><span class="pl-c1">\partial</span>(A<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> B) = (<span class="pl-c1">\partial</span> A<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> B) +_{(<span class="pl-c1">\partial</span> A<span class="pl-c1">\times\partial</span> B)} (A<span class="pl-c1">\times\partial</span> B)<span class="pl-pds">$$</span></span></td>

        <td id="L887" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="887"></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L948" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="948"></td>
        <td id="LC948" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>Let  $A$ be a hypercubical set that has $n$-box filling for all $n\geq 1$. Then in particular, $A$ satisfies contraction.  If $B\to A^\I$ has $n$-box filling for all $n\geq 1$, then in particular, $B\to A^\I$ satisfies transport.  Thus the following standard $\Id$-elimination rule will be satisfied:</span></td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC972" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>The cubical contexts will satisfy the basic cubical laws (together with symmetry) in virtue of the definitional equalities holding for the indexing projections, just as in the globular case.  The diagonals, however, will not be definitional, but only propositional.  Since path lifting holds for all dependent types, if the type of $n$-boundaries can be constructed so that the types of $n$-cubes is indexed over it,  the corollary will then imply that one has the usual box filling conditions.  </span></td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC978" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}[cf.~<span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{BCH}]  A hypercubical set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> will be said to be <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{uniformly Kan} if the following holds:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L979" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="979"></td>
        <td id="LC979" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{enumerate}</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L980" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="980"></td>
        <td id="LC980" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span>  For each open box <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^n <span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, each <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>k<span class="pl-c1">\geq</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and each map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b: <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^k <span class="pl-c1">\times\sqcup</span>^n<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, there is given an extension <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bar</span>{b} : <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^k<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> along the product map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^k<span class="pl-c1">\times\sqcup</span>^n <span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^k<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L981" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="981"></td>

        <td id="LC988" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> The chosen extensions <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bar</span>{b}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are natural in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, in the sense that for each map of hypercubes <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f : <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^j <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, one has</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L989" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="989"></td>

        <td id="LC990" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\overline</span>{b<span class="pl-c1">\circ</span>(f<span class="pl-c1">\times\sqcup</span>^n)} = <span class="pl-c1">\bar</span>{b}<span class="pl-c1">\circ</span> (f<span class="pl-c1">\times\I</span>^n),</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L991" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="991"></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L992" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="992"></td>
        <td id="LC992" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">as indicated in the following commutative diagram:</td>

        <td id="L999" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="999"></td>
        <td id="LC999" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^j <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n <span class="pl-c1">\ar@</span>{.&gt;}@/{}_{3pc}/[rrruu]_{<span class="pl-c1">\overline</span>{b(f<span class="pl-c1">\times\sqcup</span>^n)}} <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[ru]_{f<span class="pl-c1">\times\I</span>^n} &amp;&amp;&amp;</td>

        <td id="L1001" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1001"></td>
        <td id="LC1001" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{equation}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1002" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1002"></td>
        <td id="LC1002" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> The foregoing also holds for all lower open boxes <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sqcap</span>^n <span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1003" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1003"></td>
        <td id="LC1003" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{enumerate}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1004" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1004"></td>
        <td id="LC1004" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1005" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1005"></td>
        <td id="LC1005" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1006" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1006"></td>
        <td id="LC1006" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The uniform Kan condition turns the box filling <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{property} of an object <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> into an explicitly given <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{structure} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(A, <span class="pl-c1">\overline</span>{(-)})<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on the object, namely a natural choice of fillers <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bar</span>{b}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for all (generalized) open boxes <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b : <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^k<span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^n <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This will be seen to simplify the proof that the exponential <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of a Kan object  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by any object <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is again Kan. The following reformulation was arrived at in conversation with P.~Lumsdaine.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1007" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1007"></td>

        <td id="L1009" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1009"></td>
        <td id="LC1009" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A hypercubical set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is uniformly Kan just in case, for each <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-c1">\geq</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, there is given a section <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s_n : A^{<span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^n} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A^{<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the canonical map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^{i^n} : A^{<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n}<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A^{<span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^n}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i^n : <span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^n <span class="pl-c1">\mono</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the inclusion,</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L1010" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1010"></td>

        <td id="LC1073" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(A^{<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n})^X <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[rr]^{(A^{i^n})^X}  <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[u]^{<span class="pl-c1">\cong</span>} &amp; &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\ar@</span>/{}^{2pc}/[ll]^{(s_n)^X} (A^{<span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>^n})^X.</td>

        <td id="LC1102" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{def:Kanfib} By a <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{uniform Kan fibration} we mean a map of hypercubical sets <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f: B<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> equipped with a family of (upper and lower) sections <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(s_n)_{n<span class="pl-c1">\geq</span> 1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the following form:</td>

      </tr>

        <td id="L1118" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1118"></td>
        <td id="LC1118" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">there is given a diagonal filler <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c = <span class="pl-c1">\overline</span>{(a,b)}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and these fillers are moreover natural in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, in the sense that for any <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f : <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^j <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, one has</td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1129" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1129"></td>
        <td id="LC1129" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Uniform Kan fibrations are closed under <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Pi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> types along arbitrary maps, in the following sense:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1130" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1130"></td>
        <td id="LC1130" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">If <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a uniform Kan fibration, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>: A<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is any map, then the relative product <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>.B<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> along <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the right adjoint to pullback along <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) is again uniform Kan.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1131" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1131"></td>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1133" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1133"></td>
        <td id="LC1133" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1134" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1134"></td>
        <td id="LC1134" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The operation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Pi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> along a map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span> : A<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> always exists in a presheaf topos, and can  be calculated as follows:  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f:B<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>: A<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be given.  Without loss of generality, we can assume that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A&#39; =<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and calculate <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Pi</span>_A.B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, by working in the slice category over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which is also a presheaf topos.  We therefore need to show that there are sections of the form:</td>

        <td id="L1168" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1168"></td>
        <td id="LC1168" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now the arrow <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:pullbackforukf2} has a section, because <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:pullbackforukf} does by the assumption that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is uniform Kan.  Therefore <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u&#39;&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:pullbackforukf3} also has a section <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  And <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> clearly has a section, determined by the point  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(&#39;<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_A&#39;)^{<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1169" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1169"></td>
        <td id="LC1169" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s">: <span class="pl-c1">1</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> (A^A)^{<span class="pl-c1">\I</span>^n}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Thus <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-c1">\eqref</span>{diagram:pullbackforukf3} has a section <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Composing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s<span class="pl-c1">\circ</span> s&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> gives the required section <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>s_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\Pi</span>_A.B )^{i^n}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L1172" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1172"></td>
        <td id="LC1172" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1173" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1173"></td>
        <td id="LC1173" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{The universe}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1174" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1174"></td>
        <td id="LC1174" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1175" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1175"></td>
        <td id="LC1175" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">One could now construct a  model in the form of an explicit category with families, but we prefer to take advantage of the recent coherence theorem of Lumsdaine and Warren <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{L&amp;M}.  This allows us to work in a more flexible, categorical setting that has been shown to be sufficient for the construction of a CwF model if desired.  One aspect of the formulation given in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{natural} is the use of a (Voevodsky-style) universe in order to construct a so-called ``natural model&quot;, which is essentially a convenient reformulation of the notion of a category with families.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1176" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1176"></td>
        <td id="LC1176" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Here we will take a similar, if not identical approach, defining a natural transformation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p : <span class="pl-c1">\UU</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\U</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> from which one can determine a category with families in the same way as in  <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{natural}.  We first focus on the construction of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p : <span class="pl-c1">\UU</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\U</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and the proof that it is Kan.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1177" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1177"></td>
        <td id="LC1177" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1178" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1178"></td>
        <td id="LC1178" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1179" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1179"></td>
        <td id="LC1179" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be an inaccessible cardinal number, and call the sets of size strictly less than <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{small}.  Write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Set</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the small sets, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Set</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\C</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{op}}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the category of small presheaves on a small index category <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\C</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  By a <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{small (uniform) Kan fibration} we mean a (uniform) Kan fibration, in the sense of Definition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{def:Kanfib}, in the category </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1180" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1180"></td>
        <td id="LC1180" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1181" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1181"></td>
        <td id="LC1181" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\HH</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\Set</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\H</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{op}}}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1182" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1182"></td>
        <td id="LC1182" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1183" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1183"></td>
        <td id="LC1183" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> of small hypercubical sets.  We henceforth omit the qualifier ``uniform&quot; and assume that all Kan objects and fibrations are uniform; we also omit mention of the selected uniform structure.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1184" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1184"></td>
        <td id="LC1184" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1185" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1185"></td>
        <td id="LC1185" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The (<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-)<span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{universe} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p : <span class="pl-c1">\UU</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\U</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is defined:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1186" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1186"></td>

        <td id="LC1187" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\UU</span>_n = <span class="pl-cce">\{</span> (<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>, c)<span class="pl-cce">\,</span> |<span class="pl-cce">\,</span> <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span> : <span class="pl-c1">\tilde</span>{A}<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> A<span class="pl-cce">\ </span><span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{is a small Kan fibration}, A<span class="pl-cce">\ </span><span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{is a Kan object, and}<span class="pl-c1">\ </span>c<span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\tilde</span>{A}_n<span class="pl-cce">\ \}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC1198" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> Both <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p : <span class="pl-c1">\UU</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\U</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>  and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\U</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are Kan -- add the proofs.</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1199" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1199"></td>
        <td id="LC1199" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> A cubical <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-groupoid is a cubical set with box-filling operations.  The contexts over a type do form such a groupoid (``cubical Lumsdaine&#39;&#39;). Write it up.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L1204" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1204"></td>

        <td id="L1205" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1205"></td>
        <td id="LC1205" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1206" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1206"></td>
        <td id="LC1206" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> According to Grothedieck <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{PS}, the category <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\H</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a test category, and so the category <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\HH</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\psh</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\H</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has the same homotopy theory as simplicial sets.  Bas has pointed out a proof by Cisinski-Maltsiniotis based on decalage.  Dig this up.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1207" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1207"></td>
        <td id="LC1207" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1209" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1209"></td>
        <td id="LC1209" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>

        <td id="L1210" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1210"></td>
        <td id="LC1210" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> What is a hypercubical <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>, <span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-category (in analogy to the simplicial notion of quasicategory)?  Does the type theory give rise to one?</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L1216" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1216"></td>
        <td id="LC1216" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\begin{enumerate}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1217" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1217"></td>
        <td id="LC1217" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\item It can be shown that now every map factors as:</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1218" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1218"></td>
        <td id="LC1218" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\[</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1219" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1219"></td>
        <td id="LC1219" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\xymatrix{</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1220" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1220"></td>
        <td id="LC1220" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> I^n \ar[r]^{f} \ar[d]_{\beta} &amp; I^m\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1221" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1221"></td>
        <td id="LC1221" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>I^k \ar[r]_{\sigma} &amp; I^k \ar[u]_{\alpha}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1222" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1222"></td>
        <td id="LC1222" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>}</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1223" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1223"></td>
        <td id="LC1223" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1224" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1224"></td>
        <td id="LC1224" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>where $\alpha : I^k \to I^m$ is a (composite) face, $\sigma : I^k \to I^k$ is a (composite) permutation, and $\beta : I^n \to I^k$ is a (composite) degeneracy.  Using this, it can be shown that $\mathbb{C}_s$ is the free \emph{symmetric} monoidal category on an interval.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1225" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1225"></td>
        <td id="LC1225" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1226" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1226"></td>
        <td id="LC1226" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\item The presheaf category $\mathsf{csSet} = \psh{\C_s}$ of \emph{symmetric cubical sets} again has the same homotopy theory as simplicial sets.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1227" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1227"></td>
        <td id="LC1227" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1228" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1228"></td>
        <td id="LC1228" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\item The objects $I^n$ are again the $n$-fold \emph{tensor} products of the interval $I$, but not the \emph{cartesian} products, and again the geometric realization functor to topological spaces does not preserve cartesian products, but instead takes tensor products to cartesian ones. Relatedly, there is a functor $\mathsf{Hom}(X, - )$, right adjoint to the tensor $X\otimes (-)$, which is not an exponential.</span></td>
      </tr>
